## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration dv/dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The equation of motion encodes restoring forces (position-dependent), damping (velocity-dependent), and potentially external driving (time-dependent).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodically driven system)
- Mathieu-type oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (parametric excitation)
- Coupled nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (position-velocity coupling)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (exact pendulum restoring force)
- Helmholtz-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (quadratic + cubic nonlinearity with damping)
- General polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → symmetric potential wells
- Even-power position terms (x²) break symmetry → asymmetric oscillation with drift
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - c*x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (limit cycle behavior, Van der Pol type)
- Cubic position terms with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x - c1*x³ where c0,c1 same sign) indicate softening/hardening spring behavior
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates external periodic driving → look for resonance phenomena
- Product terms x*v arise from velocity-dependent forces or from coordinate transformations of rotating systems
- Position inside trigonometric function sin(c*x) indicates periodic potential (pendulum, Josephson junction)
- Parametric terms like x*cos(c*t) indicate time-varying stiffness → parametric resonance
- Odd velocity powers (v, v³) preserve time-reversal symmetry of dissipation; even powers (v²) do not
- Absence of explicit time dependence indicates autonomous system → phase-plane analysis applicable, energy conservation or dissipation

GT Equivalence Verification (PO42)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*sin(x)*v - c1*beta*v
Candidate formulas: 67

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0313132*v³ - 0.657729*v*sin(x) - 1.31546*v + 0.383671*sin(t)`

The GT has these key components:
1. `sin(t)` term
2. `v*sin(x)` term
3. `v` term (linear in v)
4. `v³` term

Let me analyze the structure. The GT contains `sin(t)`, `v*sin(x)`, `v`, and `v³`. None of the candidates explicitly have `sin(t)` or `v*sin(x)` or `v³` terms. So I need to check if any candidate can reproduce these through parameter choices.

**Key observations:**
- `sin(t)`: No candidate has an explicit `sin(t)`. Some have `cos(c*t)`, `sin(c*t+c)`, or `exp(c*t)`. Note that `exp(c*t)` with real c cannot equal `sin(t)`. But `cos(c*t)` with no phase shift can't equal `sin(t)` either. However, `sin(c*t + c)` with appropriate constants could: `sin(t - π/2) = -cos(t)` — no, we need `sin(t)`. Setting c7=1, c8=0 in `x*sin(c8*t + c9)` gives `x*sin(c9)` which is just proportional to x, not sin(t).

- `v*sin(x)`: The Taylor expansion of `sin(x) = x - x³/6 + x⁵/120 - ...`. So `v*sin(x) ≈ v*x - v*x³/6 + ...`. No finite polynomial can exactly equal `v*sin(x)`.

- `v³`: Some candidates have `log(c*exp(c*v)+1)` or `exp(c*v)` or `log(c*v+1)`. None of these can produce `v³` exactly.

Since the GT contains `v*sin(x)` (a transcendental function of x multiplied by v), I need candidates that can produce this term. Let me check candidates with `sin` involving x:

- **Candidate 12**: `c2*sin(c3*v + c4)` — this is sin of v, not x.
- **Candidate 20**: `c2*sin(c3*x + c4)` — this gives `sin(x)` (with c3=1, c4=0), but it's NOT multiplied by v. The GT needs `v*sin(x)`.
- **Candidate 58**: Same as 12 with sin of v.
- **Candidate 67**: `sin(c7*log(c8*|x|+1) + c9)` — not `v*sin(x)`.

No candidate has a `v*sin(x)` term explicitly. Could `v*log(c*x²+1)` approximate `v*sin(x)`? No — `log(c*x²+1)` is an even function while `sin(x)` is odd. 

Could any combination work? Looking for terms that are odd in x and multiplied by v: `v*x`, `v*x³`, `v*x*log(c*|x|+1)`, `v*x*cos(t)`, etc. None of these are `v*sin(x)`.

The term `v*sin(x)` is transcendental in x and cannot be represented by any finite combination of polynomials, exponentials, or logarithms in x. No candidate contains a `sin(x)` term multiplied by `v`.

Also, `sin(t)` cannot be produced by `exp(c*t)` (which is what most candidates use for t-dependence). Some candidates have `cos(c*t)` or `sin(c*t+c)` terms, but even if they could produce `sin(t)`, they still can't produce `v*sin(x)`.

Similarly, `v³` is not producible from `exp(c*v)`, `log(c*v+1)`, or `log(c*exp(c*v)+1)` exactly.

Since the GT fundamentally requires `v*sin(x)`, `v³`, and `sin(t)`, and no candidate can simultaneously produce all three (or even the `v*sin(x)` term), there is no match.

**GT:** `-0.0313132*v³ - 0.6577294*v*sin(x) - 1.31546*v + 0.38367*sin(t)`

The GT contains these basis functions:
- `v³` (cubic in v)
- `v*sin(x)` 
- `v` (linear in v)
- `sin(t)`

Key observations:
- The GT has `sin(t)` and `sin(x)` — trigonometric functions
- The GT has `v³` — a cubic power of v
- No exponentials in x or t, no polynomials in x, no logarithms

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. For a candidate to match, it must be able to reproduce `sin(t)`, `sin(x)`, `v³`, and `v` terms exactly.

**Critical issue for most candidates:** Most candidates use `exp(c*t)` instead of `sin(t)`. An exponential can NEVER equal a sinusoidal function (they are linearly independent basis functions). Similarly, polynomials in x cannot equal `sin(x)`.

Let me check which candidates have the necessary structure:

**sin(t) requirement:** Candidates need either `sin(t)`, `cos(t)` with phase shift, or some combination that can produce `sin(t)`. `exp(c*t)` with real c cannot produce `sin(t)`.

**v*sin(x) requirement:** Candidates need `v*sin(x)` or equivalent.

**v³ requirement:** Candidates need `v³` or something equivalent like `log(c*exp(c*v)+1)` — but that's a softplus, not a cubic.

Let me scan all candidates:

Almost every candidate uses `exp(c*t)` for the time dependence — this cannot match `sin(t)`. None of the candidates contain `sin(t)` explicitly.

Some candidates have `sin(c*t + c)` or `cos(c*t)`:
- **Candidate 10:** has `cos(c9*t)` — `cos` can match `sin` with phase shift? No, it has `cos(c9*t)` not `sin`. But `cos(c9*t)` = `sin(c9*t + π/2)`, so setting c9=1 gives `sin(t+π/2)` which is `cos(t)`, not `sin(t)`. Wait — it also has `exp(c4*t)`. But it still can't produce `sin(t)` from `cos(t)` alone unless... Actually `cos(t - π/2) = sin(t)`. So `c8*cos(c9*t)` with c9=1 gives `c8*cos(t)`. We need `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, but there's no phase shift in `cos(c9*t)`. So this doesn't work.

Candidates with `sin(c*t + c)` or `cos(c*t + c)`:
- **Candidate 31:** `c7*x*sin(c8*t + c9)` — has x multiplied, can't isolate sin(t)
- **Candidate 42:** `c6*x*sin(c7*t + c8)` — same problem
- **Candidate 51:** `c7*x*sin(c8*t + c9)` — same problem

None of the candidates can produce a pure `sin(t)` term AND `v*sin(x)` AND `v³` simultaneously.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** has the correct basis functions to match the GT. The GT requires `sin(t)`, `v*sin(x)`, and `v³`, and no candidate provides all three.
